put your fangs in me

by villhag

Summary

Ancient (and chronically unemployed) vampires Agatha Harkness and Rio Vidal have been strictly best friends for 600 years.

That is, until Agatha bites her.

Chapter 1

Thousands of years ago, Rio would have ruled over a castle. A proper estate on a mountain—or at least a dramatic hill. It would be a sharp, daunting expanse of land with a cliff. Always with a cliff. The kind of place you could toss a body off of, and it would look like they’d fallen from Heaven. 

There would have been hundreds of rooms and just as many servants—golden chandeliers, stained glass windows, shrines and statues with her likeness carved out of marble.

None of this was actually a hypothetical, really—Rio knew she had ruled over one of these, once—but when your age starts to number in the thousands, memories become more like fiction than fact. You’re constantly having to parse through what is real and what is imagined—

It was all a little hard to believe, really, given her current situation in New York City.

“Five thousand dollars a month for 215 square feet?” Agatha laughed shrilly as soon as they were (barely) out of earshot from the rental agent.  “Rio, I’m going to kill myself.”

“Can you remind me why we don’t just kill the landlord instead?”

Rio joined Agatha where she was currently sitting on the cement, an umbrella propped over head to shield from the sun.

In response to her very genuine question, Agatha glared at her, then gestured toward a camera that was perched on a nearby streetlight.

“The modern surveillance state, Rio,” she groaned. “We’ve been over this. Remember when I was on the CIA watchlist in the early 2000s? We couldn’t go on vacation for a decade.”

Rio frowned. “That was unpleasant.”

“Yes, it was.”

Cars whizzed by in front of them. Big yellow taxis. Trucks and tiny Kia Souls. Rio thought back to when she and Agatha traveled by horse and buggy. The streets had smelled better then, somehow, even covered in horse shit.

A rat raced by Rio’s eyes now, voyaging from one sewer grate to the next. She thought her and Agatha weren’t much different than that rodent.

They’d known each other for six hundred years, roughly. Right around the invention of the printing press. Vampires had lived well back then. Less—as Agatha put it— surveillance.

Murder was a lot easier to get away with. Riches were more material; less digital, no credit cards. If you lived forever, it was quite easy to accumulate a lot of gold, quite like a dragon.

But a little incident involving a King of England had wiped out that particular source of wealth, and then there was the Bubonic Plague, and her and Agatha had lived with a little less for much too long.

Still, she was lucky to have a friend like her.

Friend felt like too small a word to describe it, really. Partner wasn’t quite encompassing; associate was underselling it. They met over bodies; Rio had killed Agatha’s mother, infamous leader of the most notorious vampire clan in history. She’d expected Agatha, Evanora’s firstborn daughter, to naturally retaliate, but instead she’d snuck out of the dark, clapped Rio on the back as they stood over her mother’s corpse, and said:

“I think we’re going to be great friends.”

In the years since, they invested most of their time in murder. Murder for power, murder for money, murder for fun. Agatha was unquenchable, and Rio just liked to watch her work.

But as technology had advanced, their favorite hobby had gotten trickier—a stint in federal prison for Rio had turned them both off of it since the 2010s. They’d been living off their savings ever since, but even medieval gold bars weren’t safe from inflation.

“Alright,” Rio sighed. It looked like there was no other option. “I give up. We can—”

Agatha brightened, grinning wide, and interrupted her.

“Enthrall a billionaire and take all his money?”

“Yes.” Rio rolled her eyes, but couldn’t help but smile. “Don’t look so excited.”

 

***

 

It wasn’t that Rio was against creating thralls on principle. It was more… the consequences.

Creating a thrall meant there was a small chance that whoever you put under your control could eventually fight off that control, and become a vampire in their own right. And when thralls regained sentience as vampires, they tended to have only one thought on their mind—revenge.

The last time her and Agatha had created a thrall, it had been the King of England. Which, as aforementioned, had gone insanely poorly. Agatha-almost-died poorly. Rio was picking the stakes out of her for days. It was the worst day of her life. She hadn’t been interested in repeating it.

But desperate times, desperate measures.

They had to fund Agatha’s coffee habit somehow.

 

***

 

Agatha was curled up on their AirBnb couch, the NYC skyline painting a pretty picture of flickering lights into the night. She had a copy of the Forbes 30 under 30 pulled up on her phone, which Rio observed over her shoulder—and promptly laughed.

“I finally lifted the thrall ban, and you're settling for mid-twenties tech scammers?”

“Of course not,” Agatha scoffed. She slid her hand up Rio’s neck from behind, tugging at her hair and pulling her down to the couch—all without glancing up from her phone. Rio landed ungracefully by her side, the back of her scalp stinging where Agatha pulled.

“Ow . You could have just asked me to sit down.”

 “And you could be quiet for once. Neither is going to happen.”

Her words were cold, but Rio could see Agatha fighting a grin. That was Agatha, always fighting something down—stifling it into submission. And then came Rio’s job, wrenching it out of her. It being just about anything—an emotion, an idea, a corpse Agatha had just sucked dry.

This time, it was her phone.

“Hey!” Agatha scowled. “Give that back.”

“Tell me your plan first,” Rio said, holding the red iPhone to her chest. “I’m impatient.”

Agatha took this as a challenge—as she took everything—and pushed Rio down onto the couch, climbing over her body like a rabid animal, hands tugging at the device.

Her eyes shone bright, blood red. Her fangs dropped from her canines.

And oh, how Rio loved to see her like this.

“Give. Me,” she breathed hot, venomous. “ That .”

She dug her fingers into Rio’s hands. Rio felt blood prickle around her wrists.

Rio chuckled. “I’m good.”

Agatha groaned and leaned down, her lips brushing against Rio’s shoulder. Rio’s eyes went wide at the contact, her pupils dilating in seconds. They tussled like primates every so often, just to get it out of their system—rolling around on the carpet, nails digging through skin—but Agatha had never done anything as disarming as plant a kiss to her shoulder mid-game, no, that would be awfully strange; foul play, really, outside the rulebook—

Agatha’s fangs sunk into her shoulder. Rio squealed.

“What the hell, Agatha!”

She pushed the other vampire off her, and Agatha’s back thudded on the opposite arm of the couch. Blood was dribbling down her chin, and she was smiling like a wild beast. So, so pleased with herself. Rio’s heart rabbeted in her chest uncontrollably; faster than it had in years; so fast that she failed to notice that Agatha was holding her phone again, wiggling it in the air proudly.

Rio clamped her hand down on her shoulder, where blood was seeping, and gaped.

“You’re insane.”

Agatha’s grin only grew brighter. Wordlessly, she raised herself from the couch, and disappeared to the kitchen. When she returned a minute later, she was carrying a wet wipe, a roll of paper towels, and the remote control for the television. She slowly came up from behind Rio and began to clean the wound, then pat it dry.

“Sorry,” she said, but her light tone betrayed her. “I think I got a little hungry.”

Rio laughed shortly, because she wasn’t sure what else to do.

In six hundred years, Agatha had never bitten her. Not even when they had been starving in the streets of London. Not even out of excitement after they’d killed the entire mafia in Rome. Not even when Rio had gotten enthralled by another vampire, and tried to tear Agatha limb from limb. Even then, Agatha had refused to use her teeth to subdue her.

Fangs were for killing. Well, killing, and, that one other thing—

Rio reddened.

No, she definitely didn’t mean it like that.

Agatha slunk back onto the couch, remote in hand. She looked at Rio with her lip bitten, a genuinely contemplative look on her face. It was a sort of speechlessness that looked very strange on Agatha. It made Rio want to say something, anything, even though she wasn’t sure what, but before she could, the expression was gone. Replaced by an easy overconfidence.

Agatha had raised the phone screen in front of her.

There was a picture of a man on there, from the 30 under 30 list. Tommy Ashcroft . Rio’s eyes scanned his profile. Tech startup founder, based in NYC, yada yada. Nothing special. Why would Agatha care about this guy? They could fry such bigger fish. Fuck. Rio didn’t even care. Her head was swimming. Why did Agatha bite her?

“I thought you said—” she began.

Agatha interrupted her. “Keep reading.”

With a reluctant sigh, she did. And that’s when her eyes landed on the last line.

Tommy Ashcroft is the son of Richard Ashcroft, billionaire CEO of Ashcroft Oil.

Richard Ashcroft. The second richest man on planet Earth.

“Oh, Christ, Agatha.”

Chapter 2

Chapter Notes

ahh, thank you guys for all the love. i stayed up WAY too late last night writing this. lol.

I originally just wanted to read a best friends slow burn about them, but there's not too many that I could find - most fics start with them flirting/bantering/fucking immediately, which is also very fun, but I was in the mood for some classic slow burn yearning involving these two. with a side of vampires because i couldn't help myself. anyway, hope you continue to enjoy!

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Rio Vidal hadn’t always been a vampire, but she’d always slept like one—both eyes open, mind awake, barely dreaming. Her brain came out of the womb that way, on overdrive; the doctor who swaddled her wrote on her birth certificate that she had the eyes of a gargoyle. Always watching, even when the rest of her was as stiff as bone.

Agatha Harkness had always been a vampire, but she slept like a mortal. Twisting and turning and snorting like a pig in her sleep. Sometimes her noises were so egregious that Rio could hear them the room over, and would walk her way to Agatha’s just to swat her with a pillow. 

But that night—or rather day, vampires got their best shut eye from nine am to six pm—both of them were abuzz. For very different reasons.

Agatha had gone full research mode. It was her most natural state, really; one Rio had seen her occupy thousands of times before—bent over an ancient scroll, an intercepted envelope, a bloodied murder weapon, or now, a laptop. Completely, utterly consumed by whatever question she’d committed herself to.

She was on the couch in the same exact position Rio had left her hours before, only now with a bag of potato chips cradled under one arm, and creases under her eyes from staring at the screen too long. Rio suspected she hadn’t moved once—maybe except to get the chips—since Rio went to get some shut-eye.

Of course she had not gotten any shut eye. Not because Agatha was being particularly noisy, for once, but because she had left Rio in a state of utter confusion.

The bite stared at Rio in the reflection of the TV; it was barely there now—vampire skin tended to heal like that, quicker than a bat of an eyelash—but Rio found that she didn’t want it to disappear; not before they addressed it. 

She didn’t want it to fade so completely that Agatha could pretend it didn’t happen.

“Rio, finally! You’re awake,” Agatha chirped without looking up at her. She shoved another chip into her mouth, chewing noisily as she made room for Rio on the couch. “You won’t believe how good this plan is. I mean seriously, some of my best work.”

“Agatha—”

Completely ignoring her, Agatha shoved the laptop in front of her on the table, tapping the screen with her red acrylic nail. “Tommy—the spoiled CEO kid—is absolutely our way in. His company is recruiting for a bunch of roles, and by a happy little coincidence, we just happen to have resumes that match those roles. Who knew you were so talented in…” Agatha squinted at her notes. “Backend Kubernetes cluster system programming.”

Rio opened her mouth, then closed it, then opened it again. This woman.

“Agatha, I don’t even own a computer.”

Agatha crossed her arms, as if to say and?

“I’m sure plenty of Backend Kubernetes Cluster programmers don’t have computers.”

“Do you know what a single one of those words means?”

Agatha shrugged. “I don’t have to. That’s your forte. I’m going to be a…” She clicked the mousepad, and a new resume appeared. “Human Resources specialist.”

Rio snorted. For the first time in hours, an easy smile fell on her face. She couldn’t help it. Agatha was just being so… Agatha .

“Well, that’s not completely off-brand for you,” she said, crossing her arms. “You certainly do see humans as resources.”

Agatha clapped the computer shut, then reached up and tapped Rio on the nose.

“Exactly. ”

Rio’s smile fell, the shock of contact reminding her what she’d come over to discuss.

“Agatha,” she restated, trying to keep the tremble out of her voice. The other vampire cocked her head to the side, raised her eyebrows, and made an annoyed ‘ what?’ gesture with her hands. Rio sucked in a breath. “Why did you— why did you bite me?”

Agatha blinked. And there it was again, that brief thing crossing her face. Her nose scrunched just so, her eyebrows furrowed. It was a look of uncertainty, which on anyone else would be nothing to write home about—but Agatha Harkness didn’t have looks of uncertainty. They weren’t part of her facial vocabulary.

Behind Agatha’s grass green eyes, Rio could see a flurry of possible explanations run through her mind. Rio had seen this look on her before, she realized belatedly, only it happened so rarely these days, she’d forgotten what it looked like. It was the expression Agatha got when cornered. When tied up, jailed, questioned. It was her panic button.

“Oh, come on. That wasn’t a bite ,” the vampire settled on, punctuating the point with a scoff. “My fangs just grazed you by accident. I was trying to…”

Agatha’s mouth opened, then closed. She gestured awkwardly with her hands.

“Trying to…?”

“Trying to get my phone back!” Agatha groaned. “I don’t know. I wasn’t kidding when I said I was hungry. I was getting a little Bloodlust-y all day doing apartment viewings. I mean did you see the veins on our rental agent? She was all but asking to get bitten.”

Seemingly satisfied with her own answer, Agatha slid by Rio and toward the kitchen. Her silk robe fluttered as she walked, the breeze from the open window making it wisp like a cape. She seized open the fridge and grabbed a mason jar full of red liquid. Then, looking back at Rio briefly, she grabbed another jar, and poured them both out into proper glasses from the cabinet.

Agatha was a persuasive woman, but Rio had six hundred years of experience dealing with her bullshit, and she could see the crater-sized holes in Agatha’s explanation. The woman wasn’t even trying to hide how bad of an answer it was.

Which was strange, because when Agatha meant to do something, she had been planning it for days, weeks, months beforehand—leaving Rio with the empty, confused feeling that it really had been a mistake. A one-off. An accident .

“Here.”

A hand on her hip, Agatha stood in front of her, offering her a tall glass of hemoglobin.

Rio frowned at it. Agatha frowned at her frown.

“Can we seriously just drop this? I didn’t mean to do it. I just…” Agatha groaned, pinching the bridge of her nose and squeezing her eyes shut. “Yesterday was terrible. The last week has been terrible. We’re running out of money, and we haven’t been able to afford the premium stuff in months.”

She gestured toward the glass for emphasis. The blood inside it was ruddy, already turning pinkish with age.

“So sue me if you smelled good, alright?”

Rio’s mouth went dry. Did she just say—

“I’m sorry. I smelled good?”

Agatha groaned loudly. “Are you suffering from hearing loss?”

Agatha was far past annoyed—she was downright uncomfortable . It actually filled Rio with glee, seeing her like this. She was starting to get it now. Everything was becoming crystal clear. This hadn’t been some crazy ploy to mess with Rio. This hadn’t been anything, actually. This had been Agatha Harkness so desperately sick of eating discount blood from the blood bank, to the point where she genuinely had a Bloodlust Blackout and tried to chew on Rio like livestock.

“Oh my god,” Rio giggled.

“Rio, if you don’t stop laughing right now, I will stake you.”

“So you can spill more of my blood to sniff?”

“Oh, fuck you. I’m grabbing the pitchfork.”

 


***

 

With Rio’s blooming existential crisis now squashed, her and Agatha moved swiftly onwards with their plan. Well, Agatha’s plan. 

Rio would never divine something so stupidly ambitious.

“Your name is going to be Rio Valdez,” Agatha explained as they walked through the streets of downtown Manhattan, the sun beating over their hat-covered heads. “And I’ll be Agnes Wilkstone. My interview is at ten-thirty, and yours is at twelve. Did you read the notes I gave you?”

“Wait, why do you get a different first name and I don’t?”

Agatha halted on the street, turned around, and glared at her.

“Because you never respond to aliases, Rio. You just get confused and blow our cover like fifteen minutes in.”

“That’s not true.”

“Are you going to make me call you something else for the rest of the day just to prove my point?”

Rio considered it, then nodded. “Yes.”

Agatha patted her warmly on the cheek. “No chance in hell. Now pick up the pace, the sun is melting my eyelash extensions off.”

VioCroft Labs reigned at the very tip of the Financial District, tall and thin like a twenty-four story needle. The building was wall-to-wall glass, like a body where you could see all the organs. The organs in question were mostly twenty-two year olds fresh out of various Ivy Leagues, busy-bodies who wore jeans to the office, took meetings all day, and had those megawatt pearly-white smiles that only people with money did. Rio immediately detested them.

Agatha, on the other hand, was schmoozing. But when was she not? They had arrived in the door only ten minutes ago and she’d already assembled a small posse around her. All interns, if Rio had heard correctly. They were looking at Agatha in her slim-fit pantsuit like she ruled the world. Rio couldn’t really blame them.

“And then I told Steve Jobs to stuff it! ” Agatha was somehow whispering and shouting at the same time. Watching their gaping faces, she dropped her voice conspiratorially low. “But don’t tell anyone that. I’m technically still under NDA.”

“You’re amazing,” one of them said. The others fervently nodded.

Rio withheld a groan.

“Ms. Wilkstone?” The secretary had come to interrupt what would likely have spiraled into Agatha signing autographs. “Mr. Hernandez is ready to speak with you.”

Agatha laid a hand on the secretary’s back, her eyes shining red.

“Oh, wonderful.”

 

***

 

Agatha’s interview, evidently, went very well. Mr. Hernandez emerged from the room first, a dumb smile on his face that didn’t fade even as he walked back to his office. Agatha followed out soon after, her pockets mysteriously full of something where they had been empty before.

Rio raised her eyebrow, pointing at her pockets.

“What?” Agatha asked innocently. “I just felt like the candy in there needed liberating.”

Rio couldn’t help but laugh. Of course.

“Seriously? Stealing candy? Are you ten years old?”

Agatha popped a red and white mint into her mouth and grinned. “Something like that. Give or take a few thousand. Now come on, stop being so grumpy. You’re up next.”

Rio followed Agatha’s gaze over her shoulder, where a blonde woman in a no-nonsense suit was fastly approaching. Unlike Hernandez, this woman did not seem like an easy charmer. She was wearing a frown when she asked Rio to sit down, and that frown didn’t leave her face for a solid twenty minutes into their interview. In fact, it grew into a scowl.

“If I may speak frankly, Ms. Valdez,” the woman said, cutting Rio off mid-explanation about what a CPU was. Which was fortuitous timing, because Rio had zero idea. “Despite your qualifications, I feel like you do not have a great sense for backend programming.” 

Rio wanted to say no shit, Sherlock, but she knew Agatha would yell at her for sabotaging the plan or whatever later, so instead—she smiled.

“I’m sorry to hear you think that. May I ask why you’ve come to that conclusion?”

The woman blinked incredulously at her.

“Where do I start? You’ve disastrously failed every single programming problem I’ve laid out for you so far. You’ve misunderstood basic terminology several times over—I mean, recursion is a basic principle of computer science, not a genre of television—and every time I speak, it only takes a few seconds before you start staring out of the window and looking at that woman sitting in the hallway.” The lady jutted her thumb out toward Agatha, who grinned, and waved back.

Rio bit down on her lip to stifle a laugh. Jesus Christ.

She turned back to the woman, and gave her an apologetic smile. Not for the terrible interview, which was actually pretty entertaining—the vein on this woman’s forehead bulged every time Rio gave an answer—but for what she was about to do next.

“Listen.” Rio placed her hand over the woman’s own, where it was fidgeting with a pencil. The woman looked at it, stunned, but didn’t pull away as Rio’s eyes began to glow red. “This has been a great conversation. I’ve been a phenomenal candidate. I mean like, probably the best you’ve ever interviewed. I answered all of your questions perfectly, and went the extra mile with my answers. I’m super good at Kubernetes, or whatever the fuck. You’re going to go back to your boss with rave reviews about me, and tomorrow I’ll wake up with an email saying I got the job. Alright?”

The woman’s eyebrows furrowed as her own eyes began to turn red. She looked halfway between nodding yes and nodding no. 

“I’m not sure that’s true…” the woman mumbled noncommittally. “I feel like the interview went poorly, actually.”

“It is. Super true. All of it. It was a great interview. Why would it not be?”

Rio was growing agitated. Suggestion was really Agatha’s forte, not hers. She could do it, sure, but half the time her victims snapped out of it before it could really take hold.

The woman’s eyes began to clear, and her frown was returning. Damn it .

The door to the office snapped open. Long brown hair whisked in.

Agatha gave Rio a shit-eating grin.

“I’ve got this under control,” Rio muttered.

“Sure you do,” Agatha laughed meanly.

The other vampire didn’t even have to lay a hand on the blonde. She just stood there, a hand on her hip, eyebrow cocked, and the woman turned to her.

“You’re going to hire her,” Agatha said, pointing to Rio. “Okay?”

The woman swallowed hard, blinked twice, then nodded.

“Okay.”

Rio groaned. “For fuck’s sake.”

Chapter 3

Chapter Notes

YES ANOTHER CHAPTER ALREADY i am seriously going feral over these two. and now they're starting to go feral over each other. oops.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Rio hadn’t worked a real, human job in, well… It occurred to her that maybe she had never worked a real human job, at least as long as she’d been a vampire. She was sure in the twenty-two years that preceded her turning, she’d done some sort of labor. She faintly recollected pulling carrots from dirt, cleaning them, chopping them. She’d been your typical 10th century farm hand wench. Maybe? Again, memory—fickle creature. 

But not as fickle as fucking Kubernetes.

Rio inwardly groaned as she tapped fruitlessly at her mouse. She’d been downloading and re-downloading the same program over and over, but it refused to boot up. Boot up. Was that even the right word? She was so in over her head. 

Even logging into the laptop to begin with had been a chore—why is the power button a weird circle with a line through it? Wouldn’t it make more sense if it just said the word power , for fuck’s sake?—and then there was the whole ordeal with the username (this is something like an alias) and the password (like the combination for a safe.)

Agatha, meanwhile, was having a grand time. Rio knew this because she could hear her cackle of a laugh carrying three rooms over. Agatha’s job mostly consisted of conducting a ritual she referred to as “one on ones.”

Rio had asked what this term meant, and Agatha summarized it as a time for aggrieved employees to mumble their problems at Agatha, and for Agatha to quietly assure them that they were being listened to, only for her to do nothing, then repeat the same process the next week.

Apparently, hiring a human resources specialist was just the mortal equivalent of hiring a gaslighting sadist for your workplace, so really, Agatha was perfect for the job. No pretense required.

Rio was not nearly as lucky.

“Hey– uh, hi there.”

Rio momentarily paused her all-out assault on the computer mouse to drift her head in the direction of a shy little voice—one she immediately assigned to the small, curly-headed boy sitting next to her.

She hadn’t noticed him until now, but given that he was posted by his own monitor and sitting at his own office chair, he’d probably been there the whole time.

“I’m Billy.” The boy laughed nervously, sticking his hand out. Rio stared at the hand, then back up at him. He quickly retracted it. “Ah—sorry. Not everyone is a handshaker. You’re Rio right? Today’s your first day?” She squinted, then nodded. “Oh, awesome. I’m so glad to have you on the team. I mean, we’ve been totally swamped with this upcoming deadline. Having some extra muscle to push through is like, a godsend.”

“Uh huh.”

Rio was already growing disinterested. But this child was apparently her team member, so she had to at least seem polite. And maybe she could get something out of it, too.

He continued rambling. “You know, maybe you and I could get lunch together today? I could show you around the office? There’s this great view on the top floor. You can see the whole city—”

“Do you know how to download Github?”

He stared at her like she’d just grown horns.

“Sorry.” He frowned. “Github? You don’t know how to download Git?”

Shit. He already looked suspicious. Ugh. Ugh. Ugh. Rio wracked her brain for everything she knew about computers. Some kind of excuse. Her eyes widened. That’s it.

“Yeah,” she said, smiling tersely. “I’m a Windows girl. I’ve never used a Mac before.”

All confusion immediately melted away.

“Oh, of course . Well, let me introduce you to the superior operating system.”

 

***

 

“Please tell me we can quit soon,” Rio whined.

The tea kettle whistled in the kitchen as Rio rested her head on the couch, her eyes closed. She could hear Agatha’s pattering footsteps treading back and forth, back and forth. She always paced when she had a problem she couldn’t solve.

Usually it was endearing, but Rio hadn’t slept in days because of having to work human hours, and she was starting to slowly lose her mind.

“Not yet.” Water rushed as Agatha poured it from the kettle, and the scent of peppermint filled the room. The vampire’s slippers tracked across the floor to her, and soon enough green eyes were boring down on Rio. “I’ve been trying to get a meeting with Tommy all week, but he won’t respond to any of my slack messages. Some boss.”

Agatha lifted Rio’s legs and slunk underneath them, placing them back on her lap as she blew on the top of her tea. Rio made a small noise of protest, but she didn’t really mean it. They almost always sat like this—some part of them touching. Vampires were tactile animals; and Agatha even more so, even if she’d never admit it. 

Rio studied Agatha’s face as she drank. Moonlight splayed across her nose, her jaw; Rio found herself staring at Agatha’s lips as she lifted the burning liquid to her mouth, then swallowed. Watched as her neck bobbed. Listened as she made that little ah sound, smiling into the vapor.

She looks beautiful.  

Rio blinked. 

The thought caught her off guard—not because she hadn’t thought it before, she’d thought it plenty of times. 

But because she’d never thought it so intensely. With an urge attached to it. 

An urge? Rio found herself dumbfounded at her own thoughts. An urge to do what?  Rio didn’t know. All she knew was that looking at Agatha was making her fingers itch. She gripped the side of the couch, trying to knead out the tension she was feeling.

Maybe the terrible quality blood is getting to me too, she thought as her nails dug into cheap plastic. The nutritional profile probably seriously decays after sitting around for a few days. Maybe I can find a way to get some better quality blood for both of us. So we don’t…

Rio’s mind trailed off. Don’t what? What was she afraid of happening, exactly?

Agatha’s fingers began to trail absently over her calf. Rio felt it like a gun had gone off in the apartment—her chest seizing. She didn’t let it show, though. God. What is wrong with me? 

She didn’t want Agatha to think anything was wrong. One, because nothing was , and two, because that never went well. As much as Agatha liked to put on a brave face, the vampire had some deadly abandonment issues.

Consequently, their fights over the years went one of two ways—Agatha was the one to start it, and Rio waited around for her to apologize, or Rio was the one to start it, Agatha cried like a hurt puppy, and then Rio apologized for the next three weeks, feeling worse than she’d ever felt in her life.

There’s no way she is.

She’s just worried about me. She just cares.

Might as well be honest.

“Yeah.”

Erogenous. It was such a scholarly way of putting it, that Rio almost missed the fact that Agatha had just called her horny.

In, out. In, out.

“Rio?”

The other vampire’s voice sounded muffled, far away, like Rio had entered a wind tunnel.

“Rio, you’re scaring me.”

Agatha’s hands were holding her arms now, pressing down. The weight felt good. Felt grounding. Rio didn’t realize how desperately she needed to feel that way. She wrapped her own arms around herself, and shivered. Her teeth chattered, and she felt her fangs collide against molars.

So Agatha did, and she returned some vague amount of time later. Everything felt so strange —time felt gooey, imperceptible. The next thing she knew, she was waking up on the bathroom floor. Her head was in Agatha’s lap, and the other vampire was staring at her like she was the most important thing in the entire world.

It made Rio want to explode, just a little.

But she was still incredibly lethargic.

“What the hell just happened?” she moaned, closing her eyes. The fluorescent bathroom lights were like tiny stakes. “I feel like I just took fifteen shots of straight tequila.”

“I don’t know,” Agatha said, but her bitten lip said otherwise. She had that expression on her face that meant she was trying very hard to withhold something, and doing so poorly.

“Yes you do,” Rio muttered. “Out with it.”

“Err.” Was Agatha blushing? No, that had to be the light. Or Rio’s eyes. “No, I really don't. I’m no vampire doctor. I think you just got… lightheaded. We seriously need to get higher quality blood. We are way too rich to be living off Walmart hemoglobin.”

A smile crept up Rio’s lips despite herself.

“We’re explicitly not rich, Agatha.”

“We will be soon.”

Agatha had begun to dig her fingers into Rio’s scalp, itching softly. It made Rio’s entire body relax, go limp. She felt herself wading into the ocean of sleep, drifting off like a raft.

“Very, very soon.”

Chapter 4

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Rio and Agatha’s friendship had very few downsides. So few that Rio could list them all off the top of her head, and count them on one hand. 

The first was that they were the same age. Born two days apart. August 19 and August 21, which meant they were both Leos. And Rio had lived long enough to know star signs weren’t just ways to sell horoscope magazines to insecure women. No, the tradition of following the stars had actually started with Vampires; it was humans who took it and made it into subscription apps.

 Historically, if another vampire was born in your season, under your star, it meant you were destined to be at each other's throats, one way or another. It meant that her and Agatha shared strengths—and they also shared weaknesses.

They were both cocky. Agatha more so. They were both loyal. Rio more so. They were both shitty at confrontation. Great at doing the confronting, terrible at being confronted. 

The second downside was, in a way, the same as the first. They were born two days apart, yes, but Rio was born a human, and Agatha was born a vampire. That meant that for nineteen years, they received completely different educations. 

Rio learned how to harvest vegetables, and Agatha learned how to command a room of ancient blood-sucking politicians. 

Rio learned how to do basic arithmetic, and Agatha learned what it meant to bite.

Rio had been bitten only once in her life by another vampire—well, before Agatha. It had been an older man, a stranger, one that belonged to Agatha’s clan. 

Rio had expunged his name and face from her mind, drowned it in the blood of every sick creature that belonged to the Harkness clan. All who she rid the Earth of, forever.

All except Agatha.

This was all to say, she knew vampire bites to do three things—to turn someone, to kill them, or to enthrall them; to make them your slave. There was apparently a fourth, non-lethal thing bites had the potential to do, one Agatha had mentioned maybe twice in their six hundred years together, but she’d only ever referred to it as just that—a “fourth thing.” 

She refused to elaborate, even back then.

Rio had deduced that it had something to do with sex. She only guessed this because of the way that Agatha flushed whenever she brought it up, the way her hands got clammy, how her throat bobbed just a bit.

It seemed a reasonable explanation, at least superficially, that vampires might bite as some kind of erotic foreplay with a mortal victim. Personally, she had never had the urge to do so—she wouldn’t want to risk creating a thrall out of a one-night-stand.

But now, all her plausible explanations seemed to faint and die when exposed to the oxygen of reality. None of it added up in her head. Because sure, she could buy Agatha’s explanation for biting her—she was hungry, the blood-bag blood was shitty and tasteless—but what didn’t make sense was how Rio had begun to feel in the aftermath.

These… bodily shocks.

Lethargy. Faintness. Her heartbeat racketing in her chest like a heart-attack patient.

She knew what a panic attack felt like. That had not been a panic attack.

Rio knew that. Agatha knew that. And yet.

She was being, per usual, a total asshole.

 

***

 

“I don’t get why you won’t just tell me about the fourth thing.”

“I don’t get why you won’t just tell me about the fourth thing,” Agatha repeated mockingly, lowering her voice to an almost demonic grumble—a pitiful and frankly rude impersonation.

Rio nearly snarled in frustration as she tried to keep pace with the other vampire. She kept losing track of her between the undulating packs of tourists and bank workers, a dust cloud of travel bags and well-ironed suits. Agatha was weaving like a bird through the crowds, stilettos tapping like percussion instruments on pavement.

Despite appearances, Agatha wasn’t speed walking just for the purposes of being a dick. It was half past ten, and they were late to work. Agatha would tell you it was because Rio would not stop pestering her; Rio would tell you it was because Agatha would not stop evading her very reasonable questions. Either way, the end result was the same.

The imposing facade of the VioCroft office materialized before them. Having jogged ahead of Rio to avoid further conversation, Agatha yanked open the front doors of the office and—to Rio’s surprise—actually waited for her at the gates instead of rushing upstairs.

Of course, she had to ruin what minor goodwill she’d just gained by giving Rio a ridiculous bow. Like some kind of royal butler.

Rio just sighed, her fury drained by Agatha’s idiocy.

“What on Earth are you doing?”

“Being a gentleman,” Agatha said, tipping her head back up to bat her eyelashes at Rio. “Can’t have you handling heavy machinery. You might get all faint on me again.”

“By heavy machinery you mean the door?”

“It’s a pretty heavy door.”

And oh, Heaven have mercy—Agatha was driving Rio absolutely insane. The green eyed vampire was flip-flopping so quickly between charm and avoidance, humor and cruelty. Rio had known her long enough to understand this was a symptom of Agatha avoiding something, but what she was avoiding and why was completely alien to Rio. A big blank spot in her mind.

Agatha gestured for Rio to go inside, but Rio shook her head.

“Agatha.” She laid her hand over Agatha’s warm knuckles. “We need to talk.”

Agatha tried to pull away. “I’m good, actually—”

Oh, fuck it. 

Keeping her hand firmly pressed to Agatha’s, Rio’s pupils exploded into crimson. Her fangs dug against her gums. She stared straight into Agatha’s eyes, and whispered a hint of Suggestion into them. A command. Listen to me, you idiot.

Agatha snorted. Her pupils flared right back, and she smirked wildly. Rio felt a much larger punch of Suggestion pummel her in the gut. Like a tidal wave crashing on her sandcastle.

It said: We can talk about this later.

It was a true testament to just how powerful Agatha was that all the fight immediately drained out of Rio’s body, replaced with a dull, agreeable apathy. 

She nodded reluctantly, and they filed inside.

It was like she’d been unknowingly towing around three hundred pounds of deadweight on her shoulders, only for someone to quietly inform her that she could just take it all off. The spell slid off of her like a jacket, and her eyes widened, blinking at the short boy with curly-hair.

“...And that’s how I knew I was gay,” he said.

What the hell? Rio’s mind spun. How long was I out?

Billy brushed a stray tear out from under his eye, then smiled at her softly.

“You’re such a good listener, Rio. Thank you for that.”

She blinked several times, then rubbed her own eyes. They felt so dry.

“Oh, don’t cry Rio. I know my coming out story is emotional, but…”

I’m not crying, you dipshit, is what Agatha would have said, followed by and I really don’t care about your coming out story, but Rio was the nicer Leo, so she just stood, abruptly, and began to stalk towards the sound of Agatha’s laugh—it was echoing from down the hall like a banshee’s wail. Rio flung open several doors before she finally caught the right one.

“Agatha—”

“Oh, Agnes. You are a hoot.”

Rio stopped in her tracks. Agatha was sitting on the meeting table, her leg draped over a chair, practically spread eagle. A man in a tuxedo sat a few feet from her in an office chair, grinning like a wolf who had just snuck up on some livestock.

Rio recognized him immediately. The scruffy mustache, the toothpaste-white teeth, the gleaming blue eyes. He looked straight out of a dental advertisement. Or maybe an Axe Bodyspray one.

The man, who was undoubtedly Tommy Ashcroft, looked her up and down shamelessly. “Oh it’s no problem at all Agnes, I know how in-demand you are.”

Agatha laughed again, but it was too civilized and polite to be genuine.

“Oh, Mr. Ashcroft—”

He waved her off. “It’s Tommy. Really.”

“Tommy . Where were we? Lunch tomorrow, right?”

The man hummed. Rio honed in on his eyes, expecting to see crimson.

Wait. Why are his eyes blue? Shouldn’t they be red?

It hit Rio like a freight train. Agatha wasn’t manipulating him using her powers. She was doing it the old fashioned way, for whatever fucking reason. Plain old Harkness Charisma.

Probably just to see if she could. This absolute freak of nature.

“Tomorrow’s a little busy, but…” He began thumbing through his phone. Agatha leaned forward and batted her eyelashes, kicked her heel against his leg playfully. This is literal, textbook workplace harassment . “You know what, I can move some things around.”

Agatha clapped. “Brilliant! And you’ll invite Ms. Valdez, too?”

Both Rio and Tommy looked like she’d dumped a bucket of ice water on them.

“Huh?” they said in unison, looking at each other, then at Agatha, who was completely unfazed. She just shrugged, and kept that easy, gorgeous smile on her face.

“I didn’t mean to overstep. I just think Ms. Valdez could offer some insightful perspectives on the topics we were planning to discuss.”

Tommy stared at Agatha for several seconds, then laughed. “I’m sorry. I just. Let me know if I’m hearing this right. You think the IT girl has some… insightful perspectives… on how to best conduct mass layoffs without hurting your company’s brand image?”

Oh my god.

It took everything within Rio not to laugh.

Here she had assumed that Agatha had enticed the man with her sexuality. No, of course not. How outdated of Rio to guess that. They had simply bonded over being completely morally bankrupt assholes. 2025, baby. Equality for all.

“I love mass layoffs,” Rio said, because she couldn’t fucking help herself.

And maybe just a little bit because of the full-body smile Agatha gave her afterwards.

 

***

 

That entire interaction with the CEO had been so earnestly amusing that Rio completely forgot about this morning’s argument. The pair of them talked like two chirping songbirds on the way home, going back and forth about what they intended to do with the Ashcroft family money.

“I want to buy Starbucks,” was Agatha’s idea. “Privatize it, and then make it so the only person who is allowed inside their locations is me.” She snorted. “Imagine some twenty-something college idiot strolling up to the store only to run into a bouncer .” She dropped her voice, doing another horrendous impersonation of a made-up man. “No fangs, no thousand-year-old sex appeal, no entrance, kiddo.” 

Oh, how Rio adored this idiot. “Agatha, that’s like the most useless way to spend billions of dollars you could have possibly conceived of.”

“No it’s not.” She scoffed. “You’re so boring. Go ahead, tell me your boring answer.”

Rio took the bait. “I would open a bunch of wildlife rescue centers for endangered animals.” Agatha rolled her eyes, opening her mouth to interrupt before Rio continued, “And then I’d buy a personal militia and dismantle the US government. Kill the rest of the billionaires. Redistribute the wealth. Go full Karl Marx on ‘em.”

Agatha stopped in her tracks, mouth open.

“You’re serious?”

Rio snorted, and took Agatha’s hand without really thinking, swinging it in between them.

“Maybe. Or maybe I’d just hang out at the zoo everyday and feed the monkeys.”

 

***

 

This warm bubble of hypotheticals carried them to their street and up their creaky elevator, opening onto the 15th floor. They had about twelve more days in this AirBnb before they’d be forced to leave—but neither of them thought about that now. No, nothing seemed to burst the happy little cloud until the clock hit midnight, while they were lying on the couch, eating chips, watching reruns of Gilmore Girls.

“The actress who plays Lorelai is a vampire, you know.”

Rio looked at Agatha in bemusement. “Lauren Graham? Seriously?”

“Mhm.” Agatha popped a chip in her mouth absentmindedly. Rio could almost taste the salt and vinegar just watching Agatha eat it—the smell was as powerful as an acid cloud. “She’s a shapeshifter. She’s been in every sitcom under the sun. Full House. Friends. Entourage.”

“Who was she in Friends?”

“Monica and Rachel,” Agatha said, then snorted. “Kidding. She was just Rachel.”

Rio frowned. “I didn’t know shapeshifting was a power.”

Lorelai and Rory chattered in the background as Agatha set her chip bag aside.

“Sure is. One of the most powerful vampiric talents there is, actually. And all she uses it for is to be in generational sitcoms. Can you believe that?” Agatha laughed tersely. “God, I would be way more creative if I had access to that kind of firepower.”

Rio was mesmerized, not for the first time, by that murderous glint in Agatha’s eyes.

“What would you do with it?” Rio whispered.

She didn’t mean to say it like that—so low, so earnest—but that’s how it came out.

Agatha smiled like a snake. She clicked off on the remote, and the TV shuttered into darkness. Wordlessly, she turned to Rio, so their thighs were flush on the couch. Agatha’s hair was down, wild and messy, and she was wearing one of her sleep blouses, a white, unbuttoned top.

“Remember when we enthralled the King of England?”

Agatha wrapped her hand around Rio’s, pressing her fingers into Rio’s palm. It was something she did sometimes, when she was particularly excited—she used Rio’s hand like a stress ball, kneading out that extra energy.

“Yes,” Rio breathed. “Of course I do.”

“And you remember how he broke out of our spell and burned our houses and stole all the gold from our vaults and unleashed the full power of the English army on us.”

“It rings a bell.”

“Well.” Agatha clicked her tongue, and closed her eyes, as if she was traveling back in time. “If I could shapeshift, I would have turned into his wife, and kissed you right in front of him.”

Rio didn’t know what she was expecting, but it certainly wasn’t that . Agatha looked so insanely pleased with herself that Rio couldn’t help but laugh with her full chest.

“You are so—”

“Wise? Genius?” Agatha interjected, grinning like a little kid. “God, imagine his face. The love of his life making out with the vampire who made him waddle around like a duck for ten years.” Agatha was laughing uncontrollably now, and it was contagious.

Agatha gasped in offense. “I don’t kiss ladies who don’t want me to kiss them, Rio.”

“Oh yeah? But I do, in this scenario?”

“Of course you do. You’d love it.”

The way she said it was light, teasing, obviously facetious; their crazed laughter had made them manic, put them in another little bubble where nothing else existed except their minds, their endless imagination. It should have been a throw away line, a blip in the ocean.

But to Rio it felt like being shocked by an electric fence.

“You think I want to kiss you, Agatha?”

Agatha’s grin faltered. Rio had popped their bubble with a pin-needle. She looked at a complete loss, her mouth curling around words that weren’t there.

Eventually, she said, quietly, “I was only joking.”

It was an opportunity to drop it. An olive branch that would let them return to life as it was. But something inside Rio burned. 

She didn’t do well with uncertainty, and Agatha had been bathing her in it.

“But were you?”

Agatha’s throat bobbed, and her grip on Rio’s hand constricted. Agatha’s eyes had begun to burn the slightest shade of blood red.

“Rio, I..." Her eyes drifted to Rio's shoulder, then back at her eyes. "I need to tell you something.”

Chapter 5

Chapter Notes

“I need to tell you something.”

“Need to tell me what?”

“About the bite…”

Agatha’s mouth screwed up into a tiny puckered button of an expression, like a baby tasting a lemon, and Rio would have thought it was adorable under any other circumstance, but right now all she could feel was the anticipation rocketing through her—fear, undoubtedly, mixed with something else. Anticipation. Heady and urgent.

Rio’s joke-not-joke seemed to help the other vampire get over herself, because she released a breath, and chuckled dryly.

She’d use it to describe couples on the street that were too into PDA. They’re just marking all over each other, Agatha would say, and Rio would laugh, but secretly have zero idea what she was talking about. She wrote it off as some weird Harkness clan terminology.

That’s called a soul mark.”

Agatha laughed coldly. As if Rio had said something funny.

Because what was she supposed to say?

It makes me feel insane. Like I want you to devour me. Like I want your teeth so deeply inside my skin that they never come out.

“Yeah.”

They didn’t say another word to each other until the next morning.

If given the option, they probably wouldn’t have talked for a full week—maybe a month. Again, between two avoidant Leos, it sometimes became a competition to see who could endure the silent treatment the longest. Historically, it had been Agatha. Rio tended to give in first. She was just that way, a giver. 

But not now. Now, she was… speechless, really.

But they didn’t have the luxury of time to wait around. They had a very important date the next morning. One they couldn’t awkward their way around. 

And that was with Tommy Ashcroft.

So, in another first to add to the mounting lists of firsts between them, Agatha was the one to break the ice.

She did it over coffee. It was five A.M,  the sun was barely awake on the horizon outside the apartment, and neither of them had gotten a wink of sleep. Rio knew this because Agatha had been silent the whole night. No grunts or other animalistic noises. Just the soft sounds of her head rolling back and forth on the pillow, trying and failing to get comfortable.

“Do you feel… better?”

Agatha didn’t look up at Rio when she asked it. She just whisked her coffee with a tiny metal spoon, staring into the whirlpool of brown and white. 

Rio was leaning on a chair, a black robe dangling from her body, drinking her own cup. She held the hot liquid in her mouth for several seconds, thinking of how to reply.

But nothing smart or tasteful came to her. She’d been thinking about this question all night—about if she was healed now, if she was fixed—and still, she didn’t have an answer.

When Rio didn’t respond, Agatha risked a glance up at her. Her green eyes settled on the re-opened bite mark, and Rio felt her gaze like an electric current.

“It looks like it’s fading.”

Look, now they were both liars.

Rio wanted to nod and say yes , because that would be very convenient. God, she wanted so badly to nod and say yes, because then they could just put whatever this was into a corner in both of their brains and forget about it.

But then she would be lying. And Rio was very bad at lying.

But she also hated seeing Agatha look like this. Without all her usual blustering confidence.

And after all, it wasn’t like they could do it again. Doing it again meant risking doing it for real . And doing it for real was clearly a very serious thing to do—a declaration that neither of them was interested in. It wouldn’t just be stupid, it’d be beyond that.

So Rio found a middle ground.

“I think it improved things.” Not technically a lie. It had felt amazing.

“Oh. Good. That’s… good.”

They stared at each other in awkward, terrible silence.

Agatha sighed and tangled her hands through her hair. If it was a mess last night, today it was totally untameable. She knew Agatha would beat it into submission before they headed to the office, but Rio almost didn’t want her to. It framed her face so beautifully, curled around the pale flesh of her shoulders. Rio wanted so badly to put her hands in it.

No, she chastised herself. Don’t think things like that.

Why not? You’ve played with Agatha’s hair tons of times. Why should it be weird now?

Because it *is* weird now.

Great, you’re talking to yourself. That bodes well.

Oh, shut up.

At that, Agatha seemed to unwind just a smidgen—laughing lightly.

Who they’d been for six hundred years.

Rio spit on Tommy’s cold face, then slowly peeled herself off the corpse. 

She didn’t realize how deeply in the fugue state she really was until she tried to stand—and her knees buckled. Urgent hands wrapped around her middle, softly supporting her, helping her up.

“Mmyoumok? ”

Rio heard some vague murmur from behind her, but she couldn’t decipher it. It sounded like gibberish, fuzzy and jumbled. God, her head pounded. The room wasn’t spinning, exactly—but it was something close. It was pulsating , like she was drunk out of her mind at a club.

She’d felt this way before, a few select times. Her first kill; then her second; and finally, her infamous (or just famous , if you asked Agatha) massacre of the Harkness clan.

She barely remembered a single kill out of the whole family affair. Vampires called the phenomenon a Bloodlust Blackout for that reason. It’s only supposed to occur when you’re starving—so desperate for blood that your animalistic instincts are forced to pilot you like a puppet. 

But, there was one problem.

Rio was plenty fed. She’d had her normal three cups of blood for breakfast, and two more before bed last night—a completely reasonable amount, if maybe slightly on the lean side.

Oh.

Right.

Chapter 10

Chapter Notes

Act 1 (The Horny Idiots Act) has concluded. We now begin Act 2 (They're In Love Your Honor)

The next morning was more normal than it had any right to be.

They woke hazily at four in the morning—their circadian rhythms were on life support at this point—and Agatha made it to the kitchen before Rio did.

A very rare thing, as usually Agatha took an entire hour in the shower every morning. As she put it, she was “never truly ready to face the day until she’d listened to the entirety of Beyonce’s Lemonade.”

But Rio heard none of Agatha’s pitchy vocals drifting out of the bathroom that morning. Instead she heard the burbling of the coffee pot, the hiss of the burners.

Even through the dampening curtains they’d installed, Rio still felt the daylight like a sunburn as she zombie-walked towards the kitchen table. Everything felt so still—so quiet.

The exact opposite of Rio’s mind.

She couldn’t stop thinking about last night. She was being haunted by it. Over and over over, like a daydream and a nightmare combined in one, her brain sent her flickering images of Agatha—Agatha kissing her neck, Agatha dipping her fingers through Rio’s lips, Agatha groaning against Rio’s thigh—but most of all, she couldn’t stop fixating one image.

Agatha, afraid.

Afraid not of Rio, not of what they were doing—but afraid of losing her.

It shouldn’t have felt so unnerving. It’s not like it was a surprise, was it? 

She knew Agatha cared about her. 

Agatha would always take care of her when she was sick, would cover her in blankets, press her hand to Rio’s forehead and frown, cook her blood and beef stew until the pink returned to her cheeks;

 When Rio would wake up crying in the night, memories floating up of the first time she was ever bitten, Agatha would hold her;

Hell, Agatha had killed for her more times than she could count. 

Agatha was always just there, a stupid, ridiculous, overconfident constant in Rio’s life.

But Rio supposed, in the back of her mind, she had always expected that someday, Agatha would leave. After all, Agatha was a free spirit. A wanderer. She looked out for herself, and Rio didn’t blame her for that. 

Her family—may they rest in eternal damnation—had never shown her any other option.

And in the beginning, Agatha did leave, sometimes. They’d go a few years without seeing each other—Agatha busy raining terror down in Romania, Rio taking an extended hibernation in the ice pockets of Norway and Finland. 

They’d exchange letters; Agatha would send stupid little postcards— Sending my love from Bucharest prison!—and Rio would smile too fondly at them, tuck them away into her drawer, and think to herself, I hope I see her again.

Because that’s always how Rio had felt. Like every day spent with Agatha was maybe her last chance, and she would enjoy it to the fullest.

She realized that maybe she never stopped feeling that way. 

And she certainly hadn’t considered that Agatha could possibly feel the same.

But six hundred years was nothing, really, when it came to immortality. A blip in the timeline. Plenty of vampires had spent six hundred years together as mere happenstance, a convenient intersection of two ultimately diverging paths. 

But could her and Agatha be more than that? 

Did Rio want something more than that? 

Did Rio want…

Eternity?

The mere appearance of the word in Rio’s mind made her stomach lurch, and all the nausea she’d felt last night came rearing back. She groaned, holding onto the back of the kitchen chair to balance herself. 

Between the light in the room and the emptiness in her stomach, everything felt hazy and bad . She should probably sit down, before…

“Whoa, whoa.”

A hand snaked around her middle, holding her steady, and Rio’s eyes snapped up.

Agatha.

Agatha, hair tied in a chaotic messy bun, dressed in the cheesiest apron in her closet— Don’t kiss the chef. She bites —with almost no makeup on her bare, beautiful face.

Rio was here debating spending her life with this woman, and she was calling her the equivalent of one her favorite Prada handbags.

“Don’t sound so offended. You’re in very good company. Have you seen my DVD collection?”

Unfortunately, Rio very much had. Agatha had forced her to lug it around to every new apartment they’d gotten since 1995.

“You’re insane,” Rio muttered at her.

Agatha laughed softly.

“You bring it out in me.”

Rio thought this was another of Agatha’s little quips, but Agatha’s expression said something different. 

She didn’t have that mocking rudeness of her usual jokes—her lip was frowning slightly, her eyebrows creased. You bring it out in me. And do what?

She forced her mind to play out the scenario.

“Yes, hi, Agatha, friend and roommate of six hundred years. I’ve been thinking. Are you free next Tuesday? To do what, you ask? Oh nothing too big. Just figure out how to properly execute the whole mating soul-bite-ritual thing, like, *for real*, and pair off for life? Bite each other deliriously until death do us part? How does that sound?”

She could be naive, but she wasn’t that naive.

Agatha staying by her side as friends was one thing, but going, like, exclusive?  

Sexually exclusive?

There was no chance in hell. That woman saw everyone as potential food.

Rio tried to contort every thought in her head into a digestible sentence.

She failed.

“A lot on my mind, I guess.”

“Oh, shut up, you wingbat.”

Panicking because of the aforementioned “other, much scarier thing.”

It’s like becoming an inanimate object, in a way. A rock, a stone. Life does not happen to you, but around you. 

And in that way, Rio had always been envious of humans. The shortness of life creates an urgency around it. To find one’s purpose—one’s career—one’s, well…

It.  

Vampires, with their perpetually renewed lease on mortality, can afford to never consider the big questions at all. 

That was the great irony of it. 

The more life you’re given, the less motivated you are to live it.

I know, me, cooking, unbelievable. A full British, eggs and black pudding and everything. Will probably never happen again, so you might as well cherish it now.”

Rio’s legs shook as she took a seat. She forced a smile onto her face.

“I will,” she said, and never meant anything more. “Cherish it.”

Most mortals lived in constant fear of death. Which of course, Rio would allow, was mostly understandable—death meant disease, corpses, flies, and most fearsome of all (if the adults were to be believed) money for funerals —but Rio had never really understood what the big deal was.

 Ever since she was a young girl in Lugo, sneaking around the village graveyard, hiding behind stones and silently imitating the way mourners shoveled dirt into a shallow grave, Rio felt comforted in the singular ending death presented.

She liked it in the same way she’d always liked lines (they had a definitive beginning, and a definitive ending), counting (numbers always pleased her in ways people didn’t), measuring cups (she’d sneak into the kitchen just to measure milk before drinking it), and symmetry (later in life, she’d arrange corpses by height, always ascending).

It wasn’t until she approached ten years old that she feared anything at all. 

That fear, as she’d eventually come to name it—was Transformation.

It all started with an abrupt and sudden moment of loss, as most phobias do. It was her first pet—a caterpillar. Small and green and wriggly and perfect.

Rio kept it in her room in secret, in a glass jar, fed it leaves and let it climb on twigs, freed it occasionally to go on daisy walks in the field.

But then one day, as summer crested over rural Spain, her pudgy fingers screwed off the top of the jar, and Rio first encountered that thing—that something that was worse than death.

It wasn’t that it was messy, exactly—but more so that it had been completely renovated, redecorated, and refurbished. New drapes had been installed, over a dozen large potted plants distributed around the place, like some kind of Rainforest Cafe. 

If you squinted hard enough, you could see that all of Tony and Andrew’s original furniture was still there, kind of—the faux-leather couch, the mahogany kitchen table—but that it had either been covered in an insane amount of blankets and tapestries—all colored purple—or pushed into a corner to make room for a more expensive looking variation of the same thing.

It was a very strange way to describe someone, but Andrew wasn’t in the business of questioning people’s lifestyles. So he’d let his eyes skim over it.

“What do you want?” the live-in business associate drawled, looking displeased to see them, as if she was not the one illegally overstaying in their residence. The woman was wearing nothing but a robe, nearly naked, her eyes lidded like she’d just been woken up from deep sleep. 

But it was already three o’ clock in the afternoon. 

Andrew looked anxiously at Tony. Neither of them were confrontational people. Occasionally they’d gotten into a dispute with a guest, but it was usually over a cleaning fee, not their right to stay in the building permanently.

“Didn’t you get our messages?” Andrew said, trying to sound assertive, but mostly failing. The woman, even half-asleep, was very intimidating. “We’re here to get the keys back. And, er, you need to leave.” He peered into the room, and saw that it had also been entirely redecorated. Was that a gigantic DVD collection? “And all your stuff needs to leave. too.”

The woman blinked at him a few times, then groaned.

“This room’s closed. Try the other one.”

And then she slammed the door in their faces.

Andrew looked at Tony in disbelief. “Do something,” he whispered.

“What am I going to do?” Tony whisper-shouted back. “We should just call the police.”

“I don’t want to call the police.”

“Well, I don’t want two random women living in our apartment until the end of time. ”

They stared at each other for a long minute before they both deflated.

“Let’s just try the second room.”

So, with a great amount of humiliation, they dragged themselves across the apartment to the other bedroom. Luckily, Rio Garcia was already walking out of the door. She looked absolutely exhausted, her hair in a bird’s nest of a bun, but unlike her business partner, who had barely blinked at their existence, she startled like a bunny, her eyes going wide.

“Agatha,” she said, chewing her lip nervously as she kept her eyes pinned on them. “There are random men in our apartment.”

Tony laughed incredulously. “Random men—ma’am, we own this apartment.”

The other woman shouted from inside her still-closed bedroom, “Ugh, Rio, I told you they were coming, remember? Just do your—your thing. I’m choosing my funeral outfit. Actually, speaking of—dress or suit?”

A light pink sprouted on Rio’s cheeks, and she bit her lip.

“Suit,” she said eventually.

The other woman cackled. “I knew you would. You like me in one, don’t you?”

Rio’s cheeks got even redder, her throat bobbing, and she looked at Andrew and Tony with an expression that said god help me.

Tony was baffled.

They were going to a funeral? What? And—weren’t they business partners? Why were they flirting? Also, was that blood on the floor of Rio’s room? Yes, that was a giant bloodstain. Several giant blood stains. He was starting to go insane. These people were making him insane. He started getting the uncanny six sense that you develop growing up in NYC that told him someone crazy was about to try and kill him.

He grabbed his boyfriend’s hand. “Andrew, I think we should leave.”

Andrew spluttered, “What? But they’re still—”

“We’re leaving.” He headed for the door. “Bye girls! Have a good time at the funeral!”

“Thank you!” the one named Agatha sing-song’d from her room.

Once the door to the apartment was firmly shut behind them, Tony dragged a hand across his face, groaned, then turned to Andrew, dropping his voice into a whisper.

“You win. We’re talking to the police.” Andrew geared up to say I told you so, but Tony cut him off with, “I think they might have murdered someone in our bed.”

Andrew’s smile dropped.

“Oh.”

“Yeah.”

 

***

 

“Wow,” Agatha said, genuinely impressed as she waltzed into the living room, and noted the absence of two extremely nervous homosexuals. “You’re getting really good at Suggestion.”

Rio glanced up at her from the couch, which she was splayed over, one leg on the armrest, the other dragging onto the floor. She had her own suit on, a blazing white to match Agatha’s dark blue. When she looked up and saw the other woman in her outfit, gorgeous curls cascading over an open-breasted blazer, it took everything inside her not to push her up against the wall and kiss the daylights out of her.

Unfortunately, besides Agatha’s stupid rule, they had bigger problems. So she refrained.

“I didn’t get a chance to use Suggestion,” Rio said, pressing her lips together in a straight line. “So they’re probably pissing themselves halfway to the Brooklyn police station. Well, not probably. They are. I heard them talking about it in the hallway.”

Agatha looked her up and down—which, oh —then licked across her lips.

“Hm,” she said. “That’s not great.”

“Nope.”

Agatha grinned. “Wanna chase them and see who gets there first? Like old times?”

Rio barked out a laugh. “You’re a child. ”

“Is that a no?”

Rio bit down on her lip. Considered it.

“Should we take our clothes off first?”

Agatha gave her a particularly animalistic grin. Rio grimaced at her own choice of words.

“I mean—like—should we change back into our regular clothes?” she corrected.

Agatha shrugged, heading for the window, and unlatching it.

“If you want to lose, sure.” She stuck her leg out the window and onto the fire escape, then her head, and the roaring gusts blew her gorgeous curls into a frenzy. Still, she gave Rio a shit-eating grin through the fogged-up glass. “Time starts—oh, well, now.”

Rio clambered off the couch. “Agatha, what the fuck are you—”

By the time she reached the window, the other vampire was already mid-air. Agatha had jumped from the railing of the fire escape, soared ten feet, and then landed on the roof of a building, walking leisurely on the parapets. In heels .

“Oh my god.”

She was in love with an idiot.

A very sexy, powerful idiot.

She shook her head, then sighed, stepping out into the wind. “Game fucking on.”

 

***

 

“Agatha! Slow down, you cheater!” 

Agatha cackled in the distance. “No chance in hell, baby!”

It had been ten minutes of an all-out marathon, and Rio was so focused on not falling that she couldn’t even enjoy the pet name falling so easily off Agatha’s lips. 

With a grunt, she lurched off another rooftop, landing clumsily on the next before breaking out in a full sprint again—dodging exposed piping, tripping over uneven brick. 

The wind whipped her hair and the full brunt of the dusking sun bore down on her painfully, but she didn’t care. She hadn’t felt adrenaline like this since they were kids. 

Twenty years old and haunting the streets of London like a couple of goons, chasing men in the middle of night and making them leap into the river.

Sometimes you get old and you forget you can still be as free as you were at nineteen. 

With a small, nostalgic smile on her face, she continued to run—and watched as the silhouette of the police station began to rise through the fog. 

Agatha had a couple dozen meters on her still—she’d gotten a hell of a head start—but Rio was faster. She’d just have to keep her eyes on the prize, and…

Agatha dropped out of view.

Rio’s heels rocked on the edge of the building, coming to a sudden halt as she looked down. And there Agatha was, holding onto the side of the building with nothing but her fingernails, her eyes wide and terrified, her arms trembling. There had to be a three hundred foot drop below her. Just cold, hard, pavement.

“Rio,” she whimpered. “Help me.”

“Oh my god, Agatha, here, take my—”

Rio reached down in an instant, but the moment she took Agatha’s arms, the woman’s entire demeanor changed. She grinned wide and sinister. Her eyes blazed bright red.

“Thanks for the help. You’re going to stay right here and watch me win. ”

The Suggestion tore through Rio like a razor. Her arms stilled, and Agatha hopped down, letting herself fall—her feet hitting what sounded like metal only seconds later. 

There had been a fire escape below her the whole time.  

“You absolute asshole,” Rio mumbled, unable to move the rest of her body.

Agatha giggled, and blew a kiss up at her. “Takes one to know one.”

And Rio just watched as Agatha began to climb down. Her muscles twitched furiously, wanting to move, but unable to. She knew this was checkmate.

Except, seconds later, her eyes cleared. She could move again.

What the fuck?

She blinked down at herself. Agatha’s Suggestion usually put her in a stupor for hours. 

Not mere seconds. 

So it hadn’t been a fluke with Tommy.

Rio had slowly started to suspect that Agatha had been forcing Rio to do all their Suggesting as some sort of game—something to push Rio out of her comfort zone, as Agatha loved to do—but that illusion burst into flames as she looked down at her hands, flexing freely in the air. Agatha’s powers had genuinely faltered.

There was something wrong with her.

Rio frowned deeply at the thought. But when she spotted Agatha walking so casually, so cockily towards the police station, heels clicking, hair swooshing, she found that the worry in her chest was quickly suppressed in favor of another feeling.

Schadenfreude.

Rio grinned, and took an unconventional path down the other side of the building. She flanked where Agatha was walking, staying out of sight, before reappearing right in front of the doors to the police station.

The other vampire didn’t notice her until she was already climbing up the steps, then froze when she found Rio leaning against the door, arms crossed, grinning.

Agatha spluttered, “What the—how did you—”

The disbelief on her face was absolutely delicious.

Also, the rest of her. God did she look amazing in that suit.

“Someone’s off their game,” Rio taunted.

Agatha balked at her. “Am not. ”

Rio lifted herself from the door, then stepped toward her, gently clasping her fingers around the collar of Agatha’s suit. She bit down on her lip as she smoothed the fabric down. Her fingers grazed against the shirt for several long, arduous seconds.

When she looked back up, Agatha’s pupils were full. 

Not only were they full—they were staring directly at Rio’s lips. Hungrily.

Jesus Christ. Rio found it very hard to focus on what she needed to focus on. “Agatha, is something wrong with your powers?”

Agatha’s brow creased, as if she was frustrated that Rio was doing something that wasn’t related to fucking her. 

God, we’re in public. In front of the police station. Why is she so turned on?

Rio frowned. Then realized, because she had momentarily forgotten who she was dealing with, that this was Agatha Harkness. 

She’s turned on *because* we’re in public, in front of the police station.

Probably minutes away from being put in handcuffs.

She is so ridiculously insane.

Rio was so in love with her.

Agatha’s head tipped up, and thankfully she interrupted that train of thought before it could fester.

“My powers?” She huffed. “Of course not. My powers are fine.”

Rio rolled her eyes.

“Agatha.” She pulled gently at Agatha’s collar, which made the other woman emit the most distracting sound in the universe. But Rio pushed on. “Don’t lie to me. Your Suggestion didn’t work on me just now. And it didn’t work on Tommy before.”

“Ugh.”

Agatha looked up—then down—pretty much everywhere but Rio’s face—before shrugging and going, “Yeah, ok. Maybe.”

Rio frowned, because honestly, she had really been hoping she was wrong.

She took another step closer, and pushed a hair behind Agatha’s face worryingly.

“What’s going on with you?” she asked.

Agatha trembled a bit at the gesture, at Rio’s hand gently touching her face, which Rio noted away for later in her pile of unexplainable Agatha behaviors. But then she pursed her lips.

“If you must know. I’ve had a bit of a… mental block recently,” she muttered, cheeks reddening as if she was talking about erectile dysfunction. “With my powers. It’s happened once or twice before. Nothing to get your panties in a twist about.”

Rio frowned. She never remembered this happening before. Not in their time together.

“When? What other times?”

Agatha’s foot began to tap irritatedly against the pavement. 

“Ugh. Does it matter? Just—some other times. A long time ago. When we were apart. Remember, when you went up north, and I was in—”

“Bucharest, doing those social experiments on the prison guards?”

“Exactly.”

Rio frowned. “But didn’t you use your Suggestion on them for that?”

“Well, yes. But they were easy targets. Obedient pests like military officials and prison personnel are so weak minded. They follow orders like dogs.” Agatha laughed coldly. “I got myself locked up precisely so I could focus on rebuilding my power using them as pawns. And it worked.”

Rio’s eyebrows creased further. “Wait, you got yourself locked up? You told me that it was because you and that woman were spotted in the yard—” The thought of Agatha with someone else made her suddenly nauseous, even in distant memory, but she shoved it aside. “You told me that I should go up north to see the lights while you were in prison. That you wanted some time to relax and enjoy some free meals courtesy of the Poliția Română.”

Agatha didn’t meet her eyes. She waved her hand in front of her, the gesture she always did when she was eager for a conversation to be over. “And that’s exactly what I did. Two birds, one stone. I got my powers back, you saw a disappointing celestial event. Anyway, the point is, it’s all fixable. I just haven’t had the time to—well—clear my head. Toy around with some new victims.”

Rio nodded slowly, then lowered her voice to a whisper. The kind of tone you’d use with a child who’s put himself in a corner and refuses to speak, “But what do you think causes it? The… mental block?”

Agatha’s eyes slowly fell back to hers. Her entire face went impassive; frozen. She got that same look on her face that she did when Rio had kissed her. Like a thousand thoughts were caught in a traffic jam. Clearly, she knew something. Clearly, she had a theory. Agatha always had a theory. 

But it didn’t mean she was going to tell her.

“I don’t know,” she said. Shrugged. “Stress. Imminent bankruptcy.”

Rio laughed. As fucking if.

Something must have happened back then. Before Rio had left for Denmark in the 1800s. She had a vague recollection of something , but she couldn’t remember what. 

She cursed her stupid, useless mind.

Whatever. It didn’t matter. Whatever it was, it must also be happening now .

She just had to pry Agatha open a little bit more.

“Oh my god,” a voice squealed from a couple feet away. “It’s them.”

Rio and Agatha both turned at once to find Tony and Andrew staring at them from the bottom of the staircase, eyes wide, jaws unhinged.

Agatha chuckled.

Her worried expression wiped away slowly, and she patted Rio on the cheek, then leaned in towards her ear.

“Speaking of feeble minds,” she whispered seductively, and Rio’s entire body broke out in goosebumps. “Let me take a crack at these two? Might help in the healing process. ”

Rio shook her head, but couldn’t help but laugh.

“They’re all yours. Just do remember we’re standing in front of the police headquarters.”

Agatha gave her a brazen smile as she began to walk down the stairs.

“Good,” she giggled. “I love a challenge!”

Rio sighed as she watched Tony begin to back away slowly, absolutely terrified, and Agatha transform into one of her many characters—one of those myriad walls she hid effortlessly behind.

Apparently, Rio thought, So do I.
